- **Breaking ŌĆö Language:** Explicit recover bindings ŌĆö `ensure ŌĆ” recover` now requires explicit bindings in parentheses: `recover (<name>) { ŌĆ” }` or `recover (<name>, <attempt>) { ŌĆ” }`. The first binding receives the merged stdout+stderr from the failed rule execution (previously the implicit `${arg1}`). The optional second binding receives the 1-based attempt number (previously the implicit `${_jaiph_retry}`). Bare `recover {` without bindings is now `E_PARSE`. **Migration:** change `recover { ŌĆ” }` to `recover (failure) { ŌĆ” }` and replace `${arg1}` with `${failure}` (or whatever binding name you choose) inside recover bodies; replace `${_jaiph_retry}` with the second binding name. Implementation: `src/parse/steps.ts` (parser), `src/types.ts` (AST `bindings` field), `src/transpile/validate.ts` and `src/transpile/validate-string.ts` (scope tracking via `Set<string>` instead of boolean), `src/runtime/kernel/node-workflow-runtime.ts` (binding injection), `src/format/emit.ts` (formatter). All `.jh` sources, compiler tests, E2E tests, examples, and docs updated.
- **CLI:** Async branch numbers in progress tree ŌĆö `run async` branches now display a **subscript number** prefix (ŌéüŌééŌéāŌĆ”) on every output line belonging to that async branch, making interleaved output scannable at a glance. Numbers use Unicode subscript digits (U+2080ŌĆōU+2089) and are assigned in global dispatch order within the parent workflow (first `run async` = Ōéü, second = Ōéé). The subscript number is always rendered with a leading space (` Ōéü`, ` Ōéé`, ` ŌéüŌéé`) and in dim/grey in TTY mode; plain text in non-TTY / `NO_COLOR`. Two-digit numbers work naturally (`ŌéüŌéĆ`, `ŌéüŌéü`). Nested `run async` inside a child workflow gets its own numbering scope at the child's indent level. Non-async lines (root workflow, PASS/FAIL) have no prefix. A new `async_indices` field (array of 1-based branch indices, one per nested `run async` level) is added to `STEP_START`, `STEP_END`, `LOG`, and `LOGERR` events in both the live `__JAIPH_EVENT__` stream and `run_summary.jsonl`. Implementation: `AsyncLocalStorage`-based index propagation in `node-workflow-runtime.ts`, `subscriptNumber()` / `buildAsyncIndent()` helpers in `stderr-handler.ts`, event parsing in `events.ts`. E2E test with nested async workflows added. Docs updated (`docs/cli.md`, `docs/grammar.md`, `docs/architecture.md`, `docs/index.html`).
- **Fix ŌĆö Formatter:** Preserve intentional blank lines between steps ŌĆö `jaiph format` no longer strips blank lines between adjacent calls (or other statements) inside workflow and rule bodies. A single blank line between steps is treated as intentional visual grouping and survives formatting unchanged. Multiple consecutive blank lines are collapsed to one; trailing blank lines before a closing `}` are removed. The AST carries a `blank_line` pseudo-step so the emitter can reconstruct the original spacing. The parser, validator, runtime, and formatter all handle the new node type. E2E test added verifying preservation and idempotency.
- **Fix ŌĆö Formatter:** Multiline string and script bodies are no longer re-indented ŌĆö Repeated `jaiph format` passes no longer shift the inner text of `"""ŌĆ”"""` blocks, fenced script bodies, or prompt triple-quoted blocks deeper on each run. The formatter now emits body lines verbatim (without prepending the surrounding scope's indentation), making formatting fully idempotent for multiline content. Affected constructs: `const`, `prompt`, `log`, `logerr`, `fail`, `return`, `send`, and inline `run` scripts. E2E idempotency tests added for multiline strings, scripts, and prompts.
- **Fix ŌĆö Runtime:** Inbox-dispatched workflows now show parameters in progress tree ŌĆö Workflows invoked via channel routing (`channel findings -> analyst`) previously displayed bare names in the progress tree (e.g. `Ō¢Ė workflow analyst`). They now show named parameter values matching direct `run` calls (e.g. `Ō¢Ė workflow analyst (message="ŌĆ”", chan="findings", sender="scanner")`). The root cause was `drainWorkflowQueue()` passing an empty string to `executeRunRef()` instead of the inbox dispatch arguments (message, channel, sender). `executeRunRef()` now accepts `string | string[]` ŌĆö the inbox path passes a pre-resolved array of values, which are bound to the target workflow's declared parameter names and propagated through `STEP_START` events. E2E test updated to verify parameter display for inbox dispatch. Implementation: `src/runtime/kernel/node-workflow-runtime.ts` (`drainWorkflowQueue`, `executeRunRef`).
- **Fix ŌĆö Formatter:** Preserve `match` expression blocks ŌĆö `jaiph format` no longer destroys `match` blocks used in expression position (`const x = match var { ŌĆ” }`). Previously, the formatter emitted only the opening line (`const x = match var {`) and dropped all arms and the closing brace, producing broken output. The emitter now detects `match_expr` const values and emits each arm and the closing `}` at the correct indentation. Both statement and expression forms survive formatting; round-tripping (format twice) produces identical output. Implementation: `emitStep()` in `src/format/emit.ts`.
- **Fix ŌĆö Language:** Allow `${...}` shell parameter expansion in fenced script blocks ŌĆö Fenced (triple-backtick) script bodies no longer reject `${VAR}`, `${VAR:-default}`, and other shell parameter expansion forms as `E_PARSE`. The triple-backtick delimiter signals opaque shell, so `${...}` is passed through verbatim. Single-line backtick scripts still reject `${...}` to prevent ambiguity with Jaiph interpolation ŌĆö use `$1`, `$2` positional arguments there. The fix applies to both named scripts (`script name = ``` ... ```) and anonymous inline scripts (`` run ```...```() ``). Compiler test case added (fenced ok + backtick rejected) and golden AST fixture locked for a fenced script containing `${USER}` and `${PATH:-/usr/bin}`. Implementation: removed `validateScriptBodyNoInterpolation()` call from the fenced-block branch in `src/parse/scripts.ts` and `src/parse/inline-script.ts`; kept the call in the backtick branch. Docs updated (`docs/grammar.md`).
- **Breaking ŌĆö Language:** Remove deprecated constructs and relax unnecessary restrictions ŌĆö Seven independent cleanups that simplify the language and remove legacy syntax:
  1. **Require parentheses on all call sites.** `run setup` and `ensure check` are no longer valid ŌĆö use `run setup()` and `ensure check()`. Removes parser ambiguity between bare identifiers and zero-arg calls.
  2. **Allow `"${var}"` as a call argument.** The validator no longer rejects `run process("${task}")` ŌĆö quoted single-interpolation is regular string interpolation and equivalent to the bare form `run process(task)`.
  3. **Remove second `recover` binding.** `recover (failure, attempt)` is now `E_PARSE` ŌĆö use `recover (failure)` only. The attempt number was a leftover from the removed retry loop.
  4. **Remove underscore form for typed prompt field access.** `${result_type}` no longer resolves typed prompt fields ŌĆö use dot notation `${result.type}`. The runtime now JSON-parses the stored result and extracts the field.
  5. **Remove `channel <-` forward syntax.** Bare `channel <-` (forwarding the first parameter without an explicit payload) is now `E_PARSE` ŌĆö always provide an explicit RHS: `channel <- "message"` or `channel <- ${var}`.
  6. **Remove `wait` keyword.** `wait` was a legacy no-op. It now produces `E_PARSE` with the message `"wait" has been removed from the language`. Removed from parser, runtime, and reserved words.
  7. **Require `const` for assignment capture.** `name = run helper()` is now `E_PARSE` ŌĆö use `const name = run helper()`. Only `const` bindings are supported.

  Each removal produces a clear parse or validation error with a migration hint. **Migration:** add `()` to bare calls, prefix captures with `const`, replace `${x_field}` with `${x.field}`, replace bare `channel <-` with an explicit payload, remove `wait` statements, drop the second `recover` binding. Implementation: parser (`src/parse/core.ts`, `src/parse/steps.ts`, `src/parse/send-rhs.ts`, `src/parse/workflow-brace.ts`), validator (`src/transpile/validate.ts`), runtime (`src/runtime/kernel/node-workflow-runtime.ts`). All `.jh` sources, compiler tests, E2E tests, examples, and docs updated.

# 0.8.0

- **Breaking ŌĆö Language:** Match ŌĆö keyword always first, no dollar prefix ŌĆö `match` now always precedes the subject in both statement and expression positions, and the subject is a bare identifier (no `$` or `${}`). The old postfix expression form (`${var} match { ŌĆ” }`) is removed. The new uniform syntax is `match var { ŌĆ” }` for statements, `const x = match var { ŌĆ” }` for expressions, and `return match var { ŌĆ” }` for return position. Using `$var` or `${var}` as the match subject is a hard parse error with guidance: `match subject should be a bare identifier: match varName { ... }`. The AST `MatchExprDef.subject` now stores a plain identifier string instead of a bash-style `$var`/`${var}` reference. The runtime resolves the bare identifier against the variable scope directly instead of interpolating a bash expression. **Migration:** rewrite `match $var { ŌĆ” }` ŌåÆ `match var { ŌĆ” }` and `$var match { ŌĆ” }` / `${var} match { ŌĆ” }` ŌåÆ `match var { ŌĆ” }`. Implementation: `validateMatchSubject()` in `src/parse/match.ts`; `extractPostfixMatchSubject()` removed; prefix-form detection in `src/parse/const-rhs.ts` and `src/parse/workflow-brace.ts`; emitter updated in `src/format/emit.ts`; direct identifier lookup in `src/runtime/kernel/node-workflow-runtime.ts`. All `.jh` sources, compiler tests, golden AST fixtures, E2E tests, and docs updated.
- **Breaking ŌĆö Language:** Channel declarations with inline routing ŌĆö Route declarations (`->`) now belong at the top level on `channel` declarations, not inside workflow bodies. `channel findings -> analyst` declares both the channel and its route target in one line; `channel events -> handler_a, handler_b` supports multiple comma-separated targets. A `->` route inside a workflow body is now a hard parse error with guidance: `route declarations belong at the top level: channel <name> -> <targets>`. The runtime reads routes from `ChannelDef.routes` instead of workflow-level route statements, and the validator checks that every route target is an existing workflow with exactly 3 declared parameters (rules and scripts are rejected). The formatter emits `channel name -> target` in canonical output. **Migration:** move all `channel_ref -> workflow` lines from workflow bodies to their corresponding top-level `channel` declarations. All `.jh` sources, E2E fixtures, compiler tests, examples, and docs updated. Implementation: `ChannelDef.routes` in `src/types.ts`; `parseChannelLine` extended in `src/parse/channels.ts`; `->` rejected in `src/parse/workflows.ts`; route map built from `ChannelDef` in `src/runtime/kernel/node-workflow-runtime.ts`; route target validation in `src/transpile/validate.ts`; formatter in `src/format/emit.ts`.
- **Breaking ŌĆö Language:** Remove `${argN}` positional parameter access ŌĆö Named workflow/rule parameters are now the **only** way to access argument values in orchestration strings. The positional `${arg1}`, `${arg2}`, ŌĆ” `${arg9}` slots are removed from both the validator and the runtime. If a workflow declares `workflow greet(name)`, `${name}` is the only binding; `${arg1}` is now `E_VALIDATE: unknown identifier`. CLI positional arguments map to declared parameter names by position. Inbox route targets must declare exactly 3 parameters ŌĆö fewer or more is `E_VALIDATE`; the runtime binds message, channel, and sender to whatever names the target declares (e.g. `workflow handler(msg, ch, who)` ŌåÆ `${msg}`, `${ch}`, `${who}`). **Note:** The `ensure ŌĆ” recover` block previously injected `${arg1}` as the failure payload ŌĆö this implicit injection is now replaced by explicit recover bindings (see the "Explicit recover bindings" entry above). **Migration:** all `.jh` sources, E2E fixtures, compiler tests, examples, and docs updated to use named parameters exclusively. Implementation: `/^arg([1-9])$/` check and `maxPositionalSlots` removed from `validateSimpleInterpolationIdentifiers()` in `src/transpile/validate-string.ts`; `arg1`ŌĆ”`arg9` injection removed from `NodeWorkflowRuntime` orchestration scope in `src/runtime/kernel/node-workflow-runtime.ts`; inbox dispatch switched from `arg1`/`arg2`/`arg3` to positional binding against declared parameter names; CLI arg injection updated in `src/runtime/kernel/workflow-launch.ts`.
- **Language:** Optional parentheses at call sites ŌĆö `run` and `ensure` call sites now allow omitting parentheses when passing zero arguments. `run setup` is equivalent to `run setup()`, `ensure check` is equivalent to `ensure check()`. This applies uniformly to all call-site positions: standalone steps, `const x = run ref`, `return run ref`, `return ensure ref`, and `channel <- run ref`. When arguments are present, parentheses remain required: `run deploy(env, version)`. **Definitions always require `()`** ŌĆö `workflow setup { ... }` without parens is still a parse error. Arity checking works identically with the bare form (zero arguments). `jaiph format` normalizes zero-arg calls to the parenthesized form (`ref()`) for unambiguous output. Implementation: `parseCallRef` fallback in `src/parse/core.ts`, call-path routing in `src/parse/steps.ts`, `src/parse/const-rhs.ts`, and `src/parse/workflow-brace.ts`. Parser tests cover bare-identifier call sites in all positions; all existing `ref()` tests pass unchanged.
- **Language:** String/script type crossing enforcement ŌĆö `string` and `script` are now enforced as structurally distinct primitive types at every call site. The validator tracks which names are scripts vs. strings in the symbol table and rejects four invalid crossings: (1) `prompt scriptName` ŌåÆ `E_VALIDATE: scripts are not promptable; use a string const instead`; (2) `run constName()` where `constName` is a string ŌåÆ `E_VALIDATE: strings are not executable; use a script instead`; (3) `const x = scriptName` ŌåÆ `E_VALIDATE: scripts are not values`; (4) `${scriptName}` interpolation ŌåÆ `E_VALIDATE: scripts cannot be interpolated`. Valid usage (`prompt stringName`, `run scriptName()`) is unchanged. Enforcement applies in both workflow and rule bodies, including capture forms (`const x = run ŌĆ”`, `const x = prompt ŌĆ”`). A new "Types" section in `docs/grammar.md` explains the string/script distinction as the conceptual foundation of the type system. Compiler tests cover all four invalid crossings plus valid usage. Implementation: `localScripts` set threaded through `validateReferences()` in `src/transpile/validate.ts`, `localScripts` parameter added to `validateSimpleInterpolationIdentifiers()` in `src/transpile/validate-string.ts`.
- **Breaking ŌĆö Language:** Triple-quoted strings (`"""..."""`) ŌĆö `"""..."""` is now the universal multiline string form. `"..."` is single-line only; a double-quoted string that spans multiple lines is a hard parse error with guidance pointing to triple quotes. Triple-quoted strings work everywhere strings appear: top-level `const`, workflow/rule `const`, `log`, `logerr`, `fail`, `return`, and `send` (`channel <- """..."""`). `${...}` interpolation works inside triple-quoted blocks, same rules as single-line strings. This completes the four-delimiter system: `"` single-line string, `"""` multiline string, `` ` `` single-line script, `` ``` `` multiline script. Parser: shared `parseTripleQuoteBlock()` utility in `src/parse/triple-quote.ts` reused across `env.ts`, `const-rhs.ts`, `prompt.ts`, `send-rhs.ts`, and `workflow-brace.ts`. `tripleQuoteBodyToRaw()` normalizes triple-quoted content to the internal quoted-string format. Formatter: `src/format/emit.ts` detects newlines in string values and re-emits as `"""..."""` blocks. Error messages: unclosed multiline double-quotes produce guidance like `multiline strings use triple quotes: const name = """..."""`. **Migration:** all `.jh` sources, fixtures, compiler tests, golden AST, E2E tests, and docs updated. Implementation: `src/parse/triple-quote.ts`, `src/parse/env.ts`, `src/parse/const-rhs.ts`, `src/parse/send-rhs.ts`, `src/parse/workflow-brace.ts`, `src/format/emit.ts`.
- **Breaking ŌĆö Language:** Prompt triple-quoted blocks ŌĆö Prompt multiline bodies now use triple-quote delimiters (`"""..."""`) instead of triple backticks. Triple backticks are reserved exclusively for scripts. The delimiter structurally identifies content type: natural language (quotes) vs. executable code (backticks). `prompt """..."""` parses as a block prompt with `bodyKind: "triple_quoted"`. Using triple backticks in prompt context is a hard parse error with guidance: `prompt blocks use triple quotes: prompt """..."""; triple backticks are for scripts`. `${...}` interpolation works inside triple-quoted blocks. `returns "{ ... }"` works after the closing `"""` (same line or next line). Single-line `prompt "text"` and bare identifier `prompt myVar` are unchanged. AST: `bodyKind` replaces `"fenced"` with `"triple_quoted"` for prompt steps; script `bodyKind` keeps `"fenced"`. Parser: `parseTripleQuoteBlock()` in `src/parse/prompt.ts` handles `"""..."""` blocks; `parseFencedBlock()` remains for scripts only. Formatter updated to emit `"""` delimiters for prompts. **Migration:** all `.jh` sources, fixtures, compiler tests, golden AST, E2E tests, examples, and docs updated. Implementation: `src/parse/prompt.ts`, `src/types.ts`, `src/format/emit.ts`.
- **Breaking ŌĆö Language:** Script delimiters ŌĆö backtick for inline, triple-backtick fence for block. Named scripts now use single backtick (`` script name = `body` ``) for single-line and triple-backtick fence (`` script name = ```lang ... ``` ``) for multi-line bodies. The `script` keyword is kept for named declarations only. The previous double-quoted string body (`script name = "body"`) and bare identifier body (`script name = varName`) forms are **removed** ŌĆö both produce parse errors with guidance to use backtick delimiters. Anonymous inline scripts use `` run `body`(args) `` and `` run ```lang...body...```(args) `` ŌĆö the old `run script() "body"` form is removed. All scripts use shell `$1`, `$2` positional parameters; `${}` Jaiph interpolation inside script bodies is now a hard `E_PARSE` error. Single-backtick bodies containing a newline are also `E_PARSE` ŌĆö use a fenced block for multi-line scripts. AST: `ScriptDef.bodyKind` replaces `"string"` with `"backtick"` and removes `"identifier"` ŌĆö only `"backtick"` and `"fenced"` are valid. The formatter emits backtick delimiters. The existing rejection of unescaped backticks in orchestration strings is removed since backticks are now the script delimiter. **Migration:** all `.jh` sources, fixtures, compiler tests, golden AST, E2E tests, examples, and docs updated. Implementation: `src/parse/scripts.ts`, `src/parse/inline-script.ts`, `src/parse/steps.ts`, `src/parse/const-rhs.ts`, `src/types.ts`, `src/format/emit.ts`, `src/transpile/emit-script.ts`, `src/transpile/validate-string.ts`.
- **Docs:** Landing page pre-1.0 notice ŌĆö `docs/index.html` explains that core features and workflow syntax are stable since v0.8.0 while breaking changes may still occur before v1.0.0.

# 0.7.0

- **Language:** Strict scope enforcement for bare args and `${ŌĆ”}` interpolation ŌĆö both bare identifier arguments (`run greet(name)`) and braced interpolation (`log "hello ${name}"`) now enforce the same scope rules: the identifier must be a known `const`, capture, named parameter, or positional `arg1`ŌĆō`arg9`. Unknown names are rejected at compile time in both forms. The bare-argument error message no longer suggests `${name}` as a workaround, since braced interpolation applies the same strict check. Compiler tests cover both unknown-bare-arg and unknown-`${ident}` cases.
- **E2E:** Exercise `examples/*.jh` with strict assertions ŌĆö `e2e/tests/110_examples.sh` now runs every example file through the full CLI pipeline with strict `e2e::expect_stdout` and artifact assertions, replacing the previous substring checks. Examples are tracked via three arrays (`COVERED_RUN`, `COVERED_TEST`, `EXCLUDED`) forming an example matrix; an orphan guard at the bottom fails CI if any `examples/*.jh` or `examples/*.test.jh` file is unaccounted for. `ensure_ci_passes.jh` is excluded (requires real `npm run test:ci`); `async.jh` is excluded (requires real agent backends). New coverage: `ensure_ci_passes.test.jh` via `jaiph test`. See [Contributing ŌĆö Example matrix guard](docs/contributing.md#example-matrix-guard).
- **Docs:** Revisit `docs/jaiph-skill.md` ŌĆö add `match` to the Concepts bullets (Rules and Workflows) and to the Steps reference section so the agent skill accurately describes all supported constructs. Cross-checked against `docs/grammar.md`, `docs/architecture.md`, `docs/index.html`, and `src/cli/shared/usage.ts`; no other drift found.
- **E2E:** Detect and remove stale e2e samples ŌĆö five `.jh` fixtures under `e2e/` that were not referenced by any test script (`e2e/tests/*.sh`, `e2e/test_all.sh`) have been deleted: `log_keyword.jh`, `log_keyword.test.jh`, `say_hello_json.jh`, `say_hello_json.test.jh`, and `sleepsort.jh`. These files duplicated functionality already covered by wired-in tests and `examples/`, causing confusion about which samples were canonical. A new guard script `e2e/check_orphan_samples.sh` scans for unreferenced `.jh` and `.test.jh` files under `e2e/` (checking both direct references in test scripts and indirect references via other `.jh` files). Run it manually with `bash e2e/check_orphan_samples.sh` or wire it into CI to prevent stale samples from accumulating. See [Contributing ŌĆö Orphan sample guard](docs/contributing.md#orphan-sample-guard).
- **Docs:** Single architecture source ŌĆö remove root `ARCHITECTURE.md`; canonical architecture is `docs/architecture.md` only. README gains a short **Core components** section with a link to the full doc. Updated `AGENT.md`, `QUEUE.md`, `e2e/lib/common.sh`, and `.jaiph/*.jh` / `.jaiph/*.sh` orchestration prompts to reference `docs/architecture.md`.
- **Docs:** Split concerns ŌĆö `docs/architecture.md` focuses on how Jaiph is built (components, pipelines, contracts, diagrams, **durable artifact layout** as a runtime contract). JS kernel bullet now names individual modules (`run-step-exec.ts`, `stream-parser.ts`, `schema.ts`, `mock.ts`). E2E testing philosophy, normalization rules, and TypeScript test layout live in `docs/contributing.md`. Cross-links updated in `docs/testing.md`, `docs/inbox.md`, and `README.md`.
- **Testing:** Golden AST tests for parse tree shape ŌĆö a new test layer that locks in the AST structure produced by successful parses, so refactors cannot silently change tree shape. Each `.jh` fixture in `golden-ast/fixtures/` is parsed and serialized to deterministic JSON (locations and file paths stripped, keys sorted) via `serializeAstForTest()` in `src/golden-ast-runner.ts`. The result is compared against a checked-in `.json` golden file in `golden-ast/expected/`. Initial fixtures cover 8 language features: brace-if, imports, log, match, params, prompt-capture, run-ensure, and script-defs. Run with `npm run test:golden-ast`; also wired into `npm test`. To regenerate goldens after an intentional parser change: `UPDATE_GOLDEN=1 npm run test:golden-ast`. See [Testing ŌĆö Golden AST tests](docs/testing.md#golden-ast-tests) for details.
- **Breaking ŌĆö Language:** Bare identifier arguments required; standalone `"${identifier}"` rejected ŌĆö Call sites for `run`, `ensure`, `return run`/`return ensure`, `send ŌĆ” <- run`, and `const x = run ŌĆ”` now require **bare identifiers** for passing in-scope variables: `run greet(name)` instead of `run greet("${name}")`. The compiler rejects a standalone `"${identifier}"` in call arguments with `E_VALIDATE: do not use "${name}" in call arguments; use a bare identifier: ...(name)`. Quoted strings with additional text around the interpolation (e.g. `"prefix_${name}"`) remain allowed since they cannot be expressed as bare identifiers. Bare identifier arguments must reference a known variable (`const`, capture, named parameter, or positional `arg1`ŌĆō`arg9`); unknown names produce `E_VALIDATE`. Jaiph keywords cannot be used as bare identifiers. `log` and `logerr` also accept a **bare identifier form**: `log status` expands to `log "${status}"` ŌĆö the variable's value is logged. **Migration:** all `.jh` files, E2E fixtures, compiler tests, examples, and docs updated to use bare identifiers. Implementation: `validateNoQuotedSingleInterpolation()` in `src/transpile/validate.ts`, log bare identifier support in `src/parse/steps.ts` and `src/format/emit.ts`.
- **Breaking ŌĆö Language:** Parentheses required on all workflow and rule definitions ŌĆö Every `workflow` and `rule` definition must include `()` before `{`, even when parameterless: `workflow default() { ŌĆ” }`, `rule check() { ŌĆ” }`. Omitting `()` is a parse error with a fix hint. Named parameters go inside the parentheses: `workflow implement(task, role) { ... }`, `rule gate(path) { ... }`. Parameter names follow identifier rules, must not be reserved keywords, and must be unique. At runtime, named parameters are bound alongside positional `arg1`ŌĆ”`arg9` (e.g. `${task}` and `${arg1}` both work). The compiler validates **call-site arity** when the callee declares parameters ŌĆö a mismatch produces `E_VALIDATE` with an actionable message naming the expected parameters. When the callee has no declared parameters, no arity check is performed. The formatter emits `()` for empty parameter lists. Named parameters are the preferred style for new code. **Migration:** all `.jh` sources, E2E fixtures, compiler tests, examples, and docs updated to use `()` on every definition. Implementation: `parseParamList()` in `src/parse/core.ts`, `params` field on `RuleDef` and `WorkflowDef` in `src/types.ts`, `collectKnownVars()` and `validateArity()` in `src/transpile/validate.ts`, runtime binding in `src/runtime/kernel/node-workflow-runtime.ts`, formatter in `src/format/emit.ts`.
- **Breaking ŌĆö Language:** Scripts and `run`: braces out; strings or fences in ŌĆö Named `script` definitions now use `script name = <rhs>` with three body forms: (1) **single-line string** `script name = "body"` (default shell runtime); (2) **bare identifier** `script name = varName` referencing an existing binding whose string value becomes the body; (3) **fenced block** `script name = ``` ... ``` ` with optional lang tag (opening `` ``` `` on the same line as `=`). The `{ ... }` brace-delimited script bodies, `script:lang` prefix forms, and the `INTERPRETER_TAGS` hardcoded allowlist are **removed**. Language selection now uses fence lang tags exclusively: `` ```<tag> `` maps to `#!/usr/bin/env <tag>` ŌĆö any tag is valid (no hardcoded allowlist). If both a fence tag and a manual `#!` shebang are present, it is an error. Anonymous inline scripts now use body-after-parens syntax: `run script() "body"` or `` run script() ``` ... ``` `` ŌĆö the previous body-inside-parens form `run script("body")` is removed. Inline scripts support fenced blocks with lang tags for polyglot one-liners (e.g. `` run script() ```python3 ... ``` ``). `const` capture with inline scripts works with both body forms: `const x = run script() "echo val"` and `` const x = run script() ``` ... ``` ``. The `ScriptDef` AST type replaces `commands: string[]` with `body: string` + optional `lang?: string` and gains `bodyKind` (`"string"` | `"identifier"` | `"fenced"`) and `bodyIdentifier` fields. The `ConstRhs` inline script capture variant (`kind: "run_inline_script_capture"`) accepts the new body position (body follows parens, not inside them). The formatter emits the new forms. Implementation: `src/parse/scripts.ts`, `src/parse/inline-script.ts`, `src/parse/steps.ts`, `src/parse/const-rhs.ts`, `src/types.ts`, `src/format/emit.ts`, `src/transpile/emit-script.ts`. All fixtures, compiler tests, E2E tests, and docs migrated.
- **Breaking ŌĆö Language:** Prompt body: single-line string, identifier, or fenced block ŌĆö `prompt` now accepts three body forms: (1) **single-line string literal** `prompt "text"` with `${...}` interpolation; (2) **bare identifier** `prompt myVar` referencing an existing binding; (3) **fenced block** `prompt ``` ... ``` ` for multiline text (opening `` ``` `` on the same line as `prompt`). **Multiline double-quoted strings are removed** ŌĆö a `"` with no closing quote on the same line now produces `E_PARSE`: `"multiline prompt strings are no longer supported; use a fenced block instead"`. All three forms work in standalone, assignment capture (`answer = prompt ...`), and `const` capture (`const x = prompt ...`) positions. `returns` is recognized as a keyword only after a complete body form. AST types (`WorkflowStepDef`, `ConstRhs`) gain `bodyKind` (`"string"` | `"identifier"` | `"fenced"`) and `bodyIdentifier` fields. The formatter emits identifier bodies as bare names and fenced bodies as `` ``` `` blocks. Fenced blocks use `parseFencedBlock` from `src/parse/fence.ts`. Implementation: `src/parse/prompt.ts`, `src/parse/const-rhs.ts`, `src/types.ts`, `src/format/emit.ts`. Compiler tests, E2E tests, and all internal `.jh` fixtures migrated. Docs and grammar updated.
- **Parser:** Fenced-block parser utility ŌĆö new `parseFencedBlock()` function in `src/parse/fence.ts` extracts a reusable parser for multiline fenced bodies (`` ``` ... ``` ``). The function handles opening/closing fence detection, optional `lang` token extraction (e.g. `` ```python3 ``), body collection, and error reporting for unterminated fences, invalid opening fences, and content on closing fence lines. Returns `{ body, lang?, nextIdx }` for use by higher-level parsers. No downstream consumers yet ŌĆö prompt and script parsers will wire it in as a shared primitive. Unit tests in `src/parse/parse-fence.test.ts` cover basic body extraction, empty body, lang extraction, offset starting position, indentation preservation, whitespace-padded closing fences, and all three error cases.
- **Runtime:** Custom agent command support ŌĆö when `agent.command` points to an executable other than `cursor-agent`, Jaiph treats it as a custom agent backend. The prompt text is piped via stdin; raw stdout is captured as the response without JSON stream parsing. No cursor-specific flags (`--output-format stream-json`, `--stream-partial-output`, `--workspace`, etc.) are appended. The run tree displays the command's basename as the step name (e.g., `prompt echo-wc.sh "..."` instead of `prompt cursor "..."`). Custom commands participate in the normal prompt lifecycle ŌĆö `PROMPT_START`/`PROMPT_END` events, run artifacts, and `returns` schema validation all work as expected. Implementation: `isCustomCommand()` and `resolvePromptStepName()` in `src/runtime/kernel/prompt.ts`; raw stdout collection path in `runBackend()`; step name propagation in `src/runtime/kernel/node-workflow-runtime.ts`. E2E test in `e2e/tests/115_custom_agent_command.sh` using a word-count agent script (`e2e/agents/echo-wc.sh`). Landing page updated with custom agent backends feature mention.
- **Testing:** Assert error locations in txtar compiler tests ŌĆö the `# @expect error` directive now supports an optional `@L` or `@L:C` suffix to verify the line (and optionally column) reported by compiler errors, not just the error code and message substring. When `@L` is present, the runner extracts the `:line:col` prefix from the error message and asserts the line matches; when `@L:C` is present, the column is also checked. All existing error test cases in `parse-errors.txt`, `validate-errors.txt`, and `validate-errors-multi-module.txt` are backfilled with `@line:col` ŌĆö confirming that the compiler currently reports correct error locations. A meta-test verifies that a deliberately wrong `@line` is detected as a failure. The directive parser (`parseExpectDirective`) and assertion logic (`runTestCase`) in `src/compiler-test-runner.ts` are extended accordingly. Syntax: `# @expect error E_CODE "substring" @2:1` (line 2, col 1) or `# @expect error E_CODE "substring" @2` (line 2, any col).
- **CI:** npm publish on tag via trusted publishing ŌĆö pushing a version tag (`v*`) triggers `.github/workflows/release.yml`, which publishes to npm using OIDC-based trusted publishing (`--provenance`). No classic `NPM_TOKEN` secret is stored in the repo. The workflow verifies the tag matches `package.json` version before publishing. A post-publish smoke job installs `jaiph` globally and asserts `--version` and `--help` match expectations. The package is no longer marked `"private"` and declares `"files": ["dist/src/"]` for a clean publish payload.
- **Testing:** Txtar-based compiler test suite ŌĆö a new language-agnostic test format for verifying parse and validate outcomes. Test cases are stored as `.txt` files in `compiler-tests/` using a txtar-inspired format: `=== test name` delimiters, `--- filename` virtual file markers, and `# @expect ok` / `# @expect error E_CODE "substring"` directives. The test runner (`src/compiler-test-runner.ts`) parses txtar files, writes virtual files to a temp directory, runs `parsejaiph` + `validateReferences`, and asserts the expected outcome. Multi-file test cases (imports) are supported via temp directory isolation. Built-in meta-tests verify that deliberately wrong expectations are detected as failures. Run with `npm run test:compiler`; also wired into `npm test`.
- **Testing:** Extract compiler tests to txtar fixtures ŌĆö migrated 200 test cases from TypeScript test files (`src/parse/*.test.ts`, `src/transpile/*.test.ts`) into the txtar fixture format established by the previous task. Fixtures are organized by error type and single-vs-multi-module: `compiler-tests/parse-errors.txt` (74 `E_PARSE` error cases), `compiler-tests/valid.txt` (103 success cases), `compiler-tests/validate-errors.txt` (20 `E_VALIDATE` / `E_IMPORT_NOT_FOUND` / `E_SCHEMA` error cases), and `compiler-tests/validate-errors-multi-module.txt` (3 multi-file validation error cases). The original TypeScript tests remain in place ŌĆö they test internal API details beyond pass/fail and are not removed. The txtar fixtures are language-agnostic and reusable by alternative compiler implementations.
- **Testing:** Add untested compiler error paths to txtar fixtures ŌĆö wrote 38 new txtar test cases (34 parse errors, 4 validation errors) covering compiler error paths that previously had zero test coverage. New parse-error cases cover: `match.ts` (unterminated/empty/invalid patterns, single-quoted strings, missing arrows ŌĆö 9 cases), `workflows.ts` (config ordering, async parentheses, log/logerr format errors, invalid route references ŌĆö 7 cases), `workflow-brace.ts` (else syntax, disallowed steps in rules, malformed else-if ŌĆö 10 cases), `scripts.ts` (unterminated blocks ŌĆö 1 case), `metadata.ts` (array quoting ŌĆö 3 cases), `tests.ts` (unterminated blocks, deprecated mock function ŌĆö 2 cases), `send-rhs.ts` (interpolation errors ŌĆö 2 cases). New validation-error cases cover: missing/duplicate wildcard arms in `match` (2 cases). Two validate-layer paths (`ensure recover` and `const prompt` in rules) are documented as unreachable ŌĆö the parser catches them first as `E_PARSE`. The test runner now also recognizes `input.test.jh` as an entry file. Fixture totals: `parse-errors.txt` 74 ŌåÆ 108, `validate-errors.txt` 20 ŌåÆ 24.
- **Docs:** Document `jaiph format` in landing page and agent skill ŌĆö add a "Formatting" entry to the `docs/index.html` features section (under Runtime) covering `jaiph format`, `--check` for CI, `--indent`, canonical style, and idempotency. Add `jaiph format` to the agent skill (`docs/jaiph-skill.md`): new step 3 "Format" in the safe delivery loop instructing agents to format authored/modified `.jh` files before committing, a formatting bullet in Authoring Heuristics, and `jaiph format .jaiph/*.jh` in the Final Output Requirement command block.
- **Formatter:** Reorder imports before config ŌĆö `jaiph format` now emits `import` statements before `config` blocks, matching the convention that module dependencies belong at the top of the file. The canonical top-level definition order is: imports ŌåÆ config ŌåÆ channels ŌåÆ const declarations ŌåÆ rules ŌåÆ scripts ŌåÆ workflows ŌåÆ tests. This reordering behavior is now documented in `docs/cli.md` and `docs/grammar.md`.
- **CI:** Register missing e2e tests in `test_all.sh` ŌĆö add `e2e/tests/100_format_command.sh`, `e2e/tests/106_dot_notation.sh`, and `e2e/tests/107_return_managed_call.sh` to the `TEST_SCRIPTS` array so they run in CI. Also fix sort order for `e2e/tests/100_bare_identifier_args.sh` (was appended out of sequence). All e2e test scripts under `e2e/tests/` are now listed in the runner.
- **Runtime:** Add `codex` backend ŌĆö `agent.backend = "codex"` routes `prompt` steps through the OpenAI Chat Completions API via HTTP streaming, joining the existing `cursor` and `claude` backends as a first-class option. Configuration: set `OPENAI_API_KEY` in the environment (missing key produces an actionable error); optionally set `JAIPH_CODEX_API_URL` to override the default endpoint (`https://api.openai.com/v1/chat/completions`). The default model is `gpt-4o` when `agent.default_model` is not configured. Structured `returns` schemas work the same as with other backends. Implementation: `codexApiKey` and `codexApiUrl` fields on `PromptConfig`, `runCodexBackend()` HTTP streaming handler in `src/runtime/kernel/prompt.ts`, backend enum extended in `src/types.ts` and `src/config.ts`. Unit tests with mocked HTTP responses added in `src/runtime/kernel/prompt.test.ts`.
- **Language:** Bare identifier arguments in `run` / `ensure` calls ŌĆö in-scope variable names can now be passed without quoting or interpolation. `run greet(name)` is equivalent to `run greet("${name}")`. Bare identifiers must reference a known variable (`const`, capture, or positional `arg1`ŌĆō`arg9`); unknown names produce an `E_VALIDATE` error at compile time. Jaiph keywords (`run`, `ensure`, `if`, `const`, etc.) are rejected as bare identifier arguments. Mixed usage with quoted arguments is supported: `run combine(tag, "release")`. Implementation: `isBareIdentifier()` and `commaArgsToSpaced()` in `src/parse/core.ts`, `bareIdentifierArgs` tracking through `src/types.ts`, `collectKnownVars()` and `validateBareIdentifierArgs()` in `src/transpile/validate.ts`. Parser, validator, and e2e coverage added.
- **Breaking ŌĆö Language:** Unify string quoting ŌĆö double quotes only. Jaiph string literals now require double quotes (`"..."`) everywhere: `fail`, `log`, `logerr`, `mock prompt`, `const`/`local` RHS, `return`, `match` patterns and arms, `prompt ... returns`, import paths, and all other Jaiph-level string positions. Single-quoted (`'...'`) and backtick-delimited (`` `...` ``) string forms are **removed** and produce parse errors with an actionable message: `single-quoted strings are not supported; use double quotes ("...") instead`. **Exception:** `script { ... }` bodies remain opaque shell text ŌĆö normal shell quoting (single quotes, backticks, command substitution) is unaffected inside them. Escaping inside double-quoted strings: `\"` for a literal double quote, `\\` for a literal backslash. **Migration:** rewrite all `.jh` sources, tests, and examples to use `"..."` with proper escaping; there is no backward-compatibility shim or deprecation period. Implementation: `src/parse/core.ts` (`stripQuotes`), `src/parse/prompt.ts`, `src/parse/env.ts`, `src/parse/imports.ts`, `src/parse/match.ts`, `src/parse/metadata.ts`, `src/parse/tests.ts`, `src/parse/workflow-brace.ts`, `src/format/emit.ts`. All repo `.jh` sources, e2e fixtures, and examples migrated. Docs and grammar updated.
- **Language:** Add `match` expression for pattern matching on strings ŌĆö Rust-style `match` with string literal, regex (`/.../`), and wildcard (`_`) patterns. Arms are evaluated top-to-bottom; the first match wins and only that arm executes. Exactly one `_` wildcard arm is required ŌĆö missing or duplicate wildcards are compile-time errors. Works as a **statement** (`match ${var} { ... }`), as an **expression** with `const` (`const x = ${var} match { ... }`), and with `return` (`return ${var} match { ... }`). Pattern types: `"literal"` for exact string equality, `/regex/` for regex testing against the subject, `_` for the default arm. Invalid regex patterns are rejected at compile time. Implementation: new parser module `src/parse/match.ts` (pattern, arm, and expression parsing), AST types `MatchPatternDef`, `MatchArmDef`, `MatchExprDef` in `src/types.ts`, runtime evaluation in `src/runtime/kernel/node-workflow-runtime.ts`, validation in `src/transpile/validate.ts`. E2E coverage in `e2e/tests/40_nested_and_native_tests.sh`; unit tests in `src/parse/parse-tests.test.ts` and `src/transpile/compiler-edge.acceptance.test.ts`.
- **Breaking: remove `contains` keyword from mock prompt dispatch** ŌĆö The `mock prompt { if ${arg1} contains "..." ; then respond "..." ; fi }` syntax is removed with no deprecation window. Test files using content-based mock prompt dispatch must migrate to pattern matching: `mock prompt { /pattern/ => "response", "literal" => "response", _ => "default" }`. The same pattern rules as workflow `match` apply ŌĆö string literal, regex, and wildcard patterns, evaluated top-to-bottom, first match wins. Without a `_` wildcard arm, an unmatched prompt fails the test. The `contains` keyword, `respond` keyword, and `if/elif/then/fi` conditional structure are all removed from the test parser. Implementation: updated `src/parse/tests.ts` and `src/runtime/kernel/node-test-runner.ts` to generate bash dispatch using `[[ "$prompt" == 'value' ]]` (string literal), `[[ "$prompt" =~ source ]]` (regex), and `else` (wildcard).
- **CLI:** Add `jaiph format` command ŌĆö opinionated formatter for `.jh` files. Parses source into an AST and re-emits it with canonical whitespace and indentation. Supports `--indent <n>` (default 2) to control indent width and `--check` for CI-safe dry-run mode (exits non-zero when files need formatting, writes nothing). Accepts one or more `.jh` file paths; rejects non-`.jh` files and fails fast on parse errors. Shebangs are preserved. Formatting is idempotent. Implementation: `src/cli/commands/format.ts` dispatches to `src/format/emit.ts` (AST ŌåÆ source emitter). E2E coverage in `e2e/tests/100_format_command.sh`.
- **Runtime:** Auto-detect model for selected backend ŌĆö when no explicit model is configured, Jaiph now resolves the effective model through a three-step policy: (1) `agent.default_model` / `JAIPH_AGENT_MODEL`, (2) `--model` embedded in backend-specific flags, (3) backend CLI default. For the Claude backend, `agent.default_model` is automatically forwarded as `--model` when not already present in `agent.claude_flags`. Every `PROMPT_START` and `PROMPT_END` event in `run_summary.jsonl` now includes `model` and `model_reason` fields so the selection path is visible in diagnostics and run artifacts. Runs succeed without an explicit model when the backend has a compatible default; the no-model error path is actionable.
- **CLI:** Show prompt backend/model in run tree ŌĆö prompt steps now display the backend name inline: `prompt cursor "summarize the..."` instead of the generic `prompt "summarize the..."`. Completed prompt lines likewise show `Ō£ō prompt cursor (10s)` instead of `Ō£ō prompt prompt (10s)`. When the backend name matches the step kind (i.e. `"prompt"`), it is omitted to avoid redundancy. Applies to both TTY and non-TTY modes. The backend is passed through the event pipeline via the `STEP_START`/`STEP_END` `name` field (previously hardcoded to `"prompt"`). Mixed-backend runs are now distinguishable at a glance in the live progress tree.
- **Language:** Add `return run ref()` and `return ensure ref()` ŌĆö return the result of a managed call directly without capturing into a temporary variable first. The same ref-validation, shell-redirection rejection, and kind-checking rules apply as for standalone `run`/`ensure` steps. Supported in both workflow and rule bodies (with the usual `run`-in-rule restriction to scripts only).
- **Language:** Add dot notation for typed prompt fields ŌĆö `${result.field}` accesses individual fields from a `prompt ŌĆ” returns` capture. The compiler validates that the variable is a typed prompt and the field exists in the schema, with actionable error messages. The underscore form (`${result_field}`) continues to work. Dot notation is supported in all interpolation contexts (log, return, fail, send, prompt, const).
- **Runtime:** Remove unused standalone `src/runtime/kernel/inbox.ts` (legacy file-backed `inbox.js` entrypoint). Inbox orchestration is only in `NodeWorkflowRuntime`; inbox docs and architecture references updated.
- **Docs:** Interlink all pages and add ToC with "you are here" ŌĆö add active-page highlighting to the navigation panel in `docs/_layouts/docs.html` using Jekyll `page.permalink` matching and `docs-nav-active` CSS class (orange left border + bold text); ensure all 11 docs pages plus Agent Skill appear in the nav panel in logical order (Getting Started ŌåÆ Grammar ŌåÆ CLI ŌåÆ Configuration ŌåÆ Testing ŌåÆ Inbox ŌåÆ Hooks ŌåÆ Reporting ŌåÆ Sandboxing ŌåÆ Architecture ŌåÆ Contributing); add Architecture and Contributing links to the Getting Started "Further reading" section for complete cross-referencing.
- **Docs:** Shorten and refocus `README.md` ŌĆö cut detailed feature descriptions, architecture internals, and long usage sections; keep project overview, quick try, install, one concise example, and contributing pointer; link to `docs/getting-started.md`, `docs/grammar.md`, and other docs pages for details instead of duplicating content. README is now roughly half its previous length.
- **Docs:** Move `ARCHITECTURE.md` to `docs/architecture.md` ŌĆö architecture documentation is now part of the docs site with Jekyll front matter (`permalink: /architecture`, `redirect_from: /architecture.md`), added to site navigation, and all cross-references across docs and README updated. Content deduplicated with `docs/contributing.md` ŌĆö architecture page covers system structure, execution flow, contracts, and artifact layout; contributing page links to it instead of repeating those details.
- **Examples:** Add `examples/` directory with runnable `.jh` files (`say_hello.jh`, `say_hello.test.jh`, `ensure_ci_passes.jh`, `ensure_ci_passes.test.jh`, `agent_inbox.jh`, `async.jh`) matching every landing-page sample; add `e2e/tests/110_examples.sh` to exercise the examples tree in CI so doc/runtime drift is caught automatically.
- **Language:** Add `script:<tag>` interpreter tags ŌĆö syntax sugar for common interpreters so authors do not hand-write shebang lines. `script:node name { ... }` expands to `#!/usr/bin/env node`, `script:python3 name { ... }` to `#!/usr/bin/env python3`, and so on. Supported tags: `node`, `python3`, `ruby`, `perl`, `pwsh`, `deno`, `bash`. Unknown tags are rejected at parse time with an actionable error listing valid tags. Combining a tag with a manual shebang in the body is also rejected. Manual shebang remains the escape hatch for interpreters not in the built-in list. Implementation: `INTERPRETER_TAGS` map and tag parsing in `src/parse/scripts.ts`, `interpreterTag` field on `ScriptDef` in `src/types.ts`, detection in `src/parser.ts`. Unit tests in `src/parse/parse-interpreter-tags.test.ts`; E2E coverage in `e2e/tests/112_interpreter_tags.sh`.
- **Language:** Add anonymous inline scripts in workflows and rules ŌĆö `run script("body")` embeds a shell (or polyglot) command directly in a workflow or rule step without declaring a named `script` block. The body is a double-quoted string; optional comma-separated arguments are passed as positional parameters (`$1`, `$2`, ŌĆ”). Inline scripts support all forms: standalone `run script("echo ok")`, assignment capture `x = run script("echo val")`, and `const` capture `const x = run script("echo val")`. Custom interpreters work via an embedded shebang: `run script("#!/usr/bin/env python3\nprint('hello')")`. Inline script artifacts use deterministic hash-based names (`__inline_<sha256-prefix>`) so the same body+shebang always produces the same script file. Inline scripts run with the same subprocess isolation as named scripts ŌĆö no parent scope variables, only positional arguments and Jaiph env vars (`JAIPH_LIB`, `JAIPH_SCRIPTS`, `JAIPH_WORKSPACE`). `run async script(ŌĆ”)` is rejected. Implementation: parser (`src/parse/inline-script.ts`, `src/parse/steps.ts`, `src/parse/workflows.ts`, `src/parse/const-rhs.ts`), AST types (`src/types.ts`: `run_inline_script`, `run_inline_script_capture`), deterministic naming (`src/inline-script-name.ts`), transpiler (`src/transpile/emit-script.ts`), runtime (`src/runtime/kernel/node-workflow-runtime.ts`), formatter (`src/format/emit.ts`). E2E coverage in `e2e/tests/111_inline_script.sh`; unit tests in `src/parse/parse-inline-script.test.ts` and `src/inline-script-name.test.ts`.
- **Docs:** Revisit `docs/grammar.md` ŌĆö rewrite as a human-readable language reference covering prompts, rules, scripts, async calls, ensure/recover, and script isolation; fix structure (headerless overview after `# Grammar`), verify all constructs against parser and runtime source, add section transitions, and correct EBNF `send_rhs` to include bare reference case.
- **Docs:** Recreate `docs/getting-started.md` as the primary onboarding entry point ŌĆö covers install, quick try, running a workflow, workspace setup, and language overview.
- **Docs:** Revisit `docs/inbox.md` ŌĆö rewrite as a human-readable reference for channels and dispatch; fix structure (headerless overview after `# Inbox & Dispatch`), verify send/route/dispatch semantics against source code, add RHS forms table, and remove scattered implementation comparisons.
- **Docs:** Revisit `docs/testing.md` ŌĆö make human-readable and accurate; fix structure (headerless overview after `# Testing Jaiph Workflows`), verify all test constructs (mock prompt inline/dispatch, mock workflow/rule/script, assertions, capture semantics, allow_failure) against `node-test-runner.ts` and `tests.ts` source code, document escape sequence support for quoted strings, and improve readability.
- **Docs:** Revisit `docs/configuration.md` ŌĆö improve readability and structure; reorganize into clearer sections (in-file config blocks, config keys reference, precedence in detail); verify all config keys, defaults, env variable mappings, and locked variable behavior against `env.ts`, `metadata.ts`, `prompt.ts`, and `node-workflow-runtime.ts` source code; add section introductions and practical context.
- **Docs:** Revisit `docs/hooks.md` ŌĆö improve readability and structure; replace inline lists with tables for config locations and payload fields; verify all hook events, payload fields, precedence logic, and execution behavior against `hooks.ts`, `run.ts`, `stderr-handler.ts`, and `types.ts` source code; tighten wording throughout.
- **Docs:** Revisit `docs/sandboxing.md` ŌĆö rewrite as a human-readable sandboxing reference; fix structure (headerless overview after `# Sandboxing`), remove redundant `## Overview` sub-header, tighten rules section into a concise explanation of the permitted step set and runtime behavior, streamline Docker section with cleaner mount specification table, simplified container layout diagram, and consolidated runtime behavior descriptions; verify all Docker configuration keys, defaults, mount parsing, Dockerfile detection, environment variable forwarding, path remapping, and container lifecycle against `src/runtime/docker.ts` and `src/cli/commands/run.ts` source code; improve readability throughout.
- **Docs:** Revisit `docs/cli.md` ŌĆö improve readability and structure; rename shorthand section to "File shorthand", promote argument passing and shebang execution to their own sub-headers, separate compile-time and process model into a dedicated sub-section under `jaiph run`; reorganize environment variables into grouped categories (internal, workspace, agent, execution, heartbeat, Docker) with sub-headings; streamline overview paragraph; verify all commands, flags, and env variables against `src/cli/*` and `src/cli/shared/usage.ts` source code.
- **Docs:** Revisit `docs/contributing.md` ŌĆö remove duplicated architecture content (artifact layout details, full-equality contract rationale, tree-vs-artifact explanation) and replace with links to the Architecture page; consolidate three E2E assertion subsections into a single concise "Assertion policy" section; verify all build/test commands against `package.json`; keep contributor-focused content (code philosophy, testing philosophy, helper reference, module test inventory) intact.

# 0.6.0

## Summary

- **Runtime:** `jaiph run` and `jaiph test` execute through the Node workflow runtime (`NodeWorkflowRuntime`) only ŌĆö no bash workflow transpilation on the execution path; Docker uses the same Node runner; `jaiph build` is no longer a user-facing command; `jaiph test` uses a pure Node test runner. Legacy `jaiph_stdlib.sh` workflow orchestration and user-facing workflow `.sh` output are gone from the runtime path.
- **Scripts vs orchestration:** Bash, polyglot shebangs, and arbitrary shell live only in top-level `script { }` blocks (opaque bodies; the compiler does not parse them as Jaiph steps). Workflow and rule bodies are Jaiph steps only ŌĆö no raw shell lines; rules may `run` scripts only (not workflows).
- **Breaking changes:** Call sites require parentheses; definitions use `rule` / `script` / `workflow` **without** empty `()` before `{`; orchestration strings allow only `${identifier}` interpolation; `mock function` ŌåÆ `mock script`; `.jph` removed ŌĆö see the detailed entries below.

## All changes

- **Fix: Treat script bodies as opaque bash** ŌĆö The compiler no longer parses `script { ŌĆ” }` bodies as Jaiph steps, rejects keywords like `const` or `fail`, strips outer quotes from commands, or validates cross-script calls line-by-line. All script bodies ŌĆö bash and polyglot ŌĆö are now opaque text to the compiler, which means embedded `node -e` heredocs, inline Python, `const` assignments in JS, and any other valid shell construct compile without interference. For bash scripts (no shebang or `#!/usr/bin/env bash`), the emitter still applies lightweight transforms: `return` normalization, `local`/`export`/`readonly` spacing, and import alias resolution (`alias.name` ŌåÆ `symbol::name`). Non-bash scripts (custom shebang) emit the body verbatim. Previously, line-based rules such as "`const` is not allowed in script bodies" caused false positives for real scripts where a line began with `const` inside embedded JS/Python.
- **CI: Verify landing-page samples (Playwright)** ŌĆö The `docs-local` CI job now builds Jaiph, installs Playwright (Chromium), and runs `npx playwright test` against the locally served Jekyll site. The Playwright suite (`tests/e2e-samples/landing-page.spec.ts`) extracts sample source and expected output from the landing page using `data-sample` DOM attributes, compares source blocks against checked-in `examples/*.jh` files, and runs deterministic samples through the CLI to verify that displayed output matches actual behavior. A new `npm run test:samples` script provides the same check locally. The landing page (`docs/index.html`) now carries stable `data-sample`, `data-sample-file`, `data-sample-source`, and `data-sample-output` attributes on each tab panel for reliable extraction.
- **CI: Getting started (local) ŌĆö Jekyll smoke-check job** ŌĆö New CI job `docs-local` ("Getting started (local)") builds and serves the Jekyll documentation site locally on `127.0.0.1:4000` using Ruby 3.2 with `bundler-cache`, waits up to 30 seconds for the server to respond, then asserts HTTP 200 on `/` and `/getting-started` via `curl`. Runs on `ubuntu-latest` only (no OS matrix). The job has no dependency on `jaiph.org` ŌĆö it validates the docs site entirely from the repository `docs/` directory. Future tasks will extend this job with sample verification against the served HTML.
- **E2E: verify `*.test.jh` testing end-to-end (`105_test_jh_verification.sh`)** ŌĆö New dedicated E2E test that exercises `jaiph test` across four scenarios: (1) a representative passing test file using `import`, `mock prompt`, `mock rule`, `mock workflow`, `mock script`, and `expectContain` with full output verification; (2) a deliberately failing test asserting non-zero exit and the expected failure report format (`expectEqual` mismatch diff); (3) rejection of the deprecated `mock function` syntax with a migration error containing `"mock function" is no longer supported; use "mock script"`; (4) directory discovery (`jaiph test <dir>`) finding and running multiple `*.test.jh` files. Acts as a regression gate for the test runner contract after the `mock function` ŌåÆ `mock script` rename.
- **Fix: `JAIPH_LIB` not inherited from parent shell** ŌĆö `resolveRuntimeEnv` now deletes `JAIPH_LIB` from the inherited environment before launching `jaiph run` or `jaiph test`, matching the existing treatment of `JAIPH_SCRIPTS` and `JAIPH_RUN_STEP_MODULE`. The Node runtime defaults `JAIPH_LIB` to `<JAIPH_WORKSPACE>/.jaiph/lib` when unset. Previously, a parent shell exporting `JAIPH_LIB` (pointing to a different workspace) would silently override the per-workspace default, causing `source "$JAIPH_LIB/ŌĆ”"` in scripts to resolve against the wrong project.
- **Fix: add `JAIPH_WORKSPACE` to unit test env for `NodeWorkflowRuntime`** ŌĆö The `node-workflow-runtime.artifacts.test.ts` recover-payload test now includes `JAIPH_WORKSPACE` in the env map passed to `NodeWorkflowRuntime`, matching the contract that `resolveRuntimeEnv` establishes for real CLI runs. Without it, workspace-dependent defaults (e.g. `JAIPH_LIB`) could resolve incorrectly in test isolation.
- **Breaking: definition/call syntax ŌĆö no parens on defs, call parens required** ŌĆö Top-level definitions (`rule`, `script`, `workflow`) must **not** use parentheses after the identifier: `rule name { ŌĆ” }`, `script name { ŌĆ” }`, `workflow name { ŌĆ” }`. Forms with `()` on definitions (e.g. `rule foo() { ŌĆ” }`) are rejected at parse time with `E_PARSE` and a fix hint. **Call sites** now **always** require parentheses ŌĆö either empty `()` for zero-argument calls or comma-separated arguments inside `(...)`: `ensure check()`, `run helper("arg1", "arg2")`, `run other_workflow()`. This applies uniformly to `run`, `ensure`, `run async`, brace `if` conditions, inline capture interpolation (`${run ref()}`, `${ensure ref()}`), and send RHS (`channel <- run fmt()`). The previous syntax that allowed bare calls without parentheses (e.g. `ensure my_rule`, `run my_script "arg"`) is no longer accepted. This change makes arity visible at every call site and removes the misleading empty `()` on definitions that never declared real parameters. All internal `.jh` sources, fixtures, E2E tests, and documentation are migrated to the new shape. **Supersedes** the earlier "`rule`, `script`, and `workflow` require `()` before `{`" entry below.
- **Feat: inline capture interpolation `${run ...}` / `${ensure ...}`** ŌĆö Orchestration strings (`log`, `logerr`, `fail`, `prompt`, `return`, send literals, `const` RHS expressions) now support **inline managed captures**. Write `log "Got: ${run some_script}"` or `log "Status: ${ensure check_ok}"` instead of extracting one-time values into temporary variables. At runtime, each inline capture executes as a managed call and the result replaces the interpolation expression; regular `${var}` interpolation applies after all captures resolve. If any inline capture fails, the enclosing step fails immediately. **Validation:** inline capture references follow the same rules as standalone `run` / `ensure` steps (correct target kind, no shell redirection). **Nested inline captures** (e.g. `${run foo ${run bar}}`) and **invalid references** (e.g. `${run 123bad}`) are rejected at compile time with `E_PARSE`. Covered by unit tests (`validate-string.test.ts`) and E2E tests (`100_inline_capture_interpolation.sh`) across runtime execution, failure propagation, mixed interpolation, `jaiph test` integration, and compile-time rejection of nested/invalid forms.
- **E2E: verify custom shebang polyglot scripts for Python and Node** ŌĆö `e2e/tests/92_custom_shebang_polyglot.sh` now exercises **both** `#!/usr/bin/env python3` and `#!/usr/bin/env node` shebangs in separate sections. Each interpreter gets its own test environment and fixture (`polyglot.jh` for Python, `polyglot_node.jh` for Node), asserting full CLI stdout and artifact file counts. When an interpreter is not in `PATH`, its section is skipped with `e2e::skip` ŌĆö the test no longer exits early on a missing `python3`, so both interpreters are tested independently.
- **E2E tests: migrate to full-output and full-artifact contracts** ŌĆö Converted 28 `e2e::assert_contains` calls across 8 test files (`30_filesystem_side_effects.sh`, `74_live_step_output.sh`, `91_inbox_dispatch.sh`, `92_log_logerr.sh`, `93_inbox_stress.sh`, `97_step_output_contract.sh`, `98_ensure_recover_value.sh`, `101_script_isolation.sh`) to `e2e::assert_equals` with full expected content. Side-effect files, `.out`/`.err` artifacts, and inbox file contents now use exact-match assertions instead of substring checks. Remaining `assert_contains` usages are categorized as justified exceptions (nondeterministic output, unbounded logs, platform-dependent text) with inline comments, or tracked as convertible in `docs/contributing.md`. The default E2E contract ŌĆö full equality on CLI stdout, artifact files, and inbox contents ŌĆö is documented in ARCHITECTURE.md, `docs/contributing.md`, `docs/testing.md`, `e2e/lib/common.sh`, and the `.jaiph/engineer.jh` / `.jaiph/qa.jh` orchestration workflows.
- **Remove workflow bash transpilation and source maps** ŌĆö The compiler no longer emits workflow-level bash, `build()`, `transpileFile()`, or `.jaiph.map` sidecars. The only build output is **`buildScripts()`** ŌåÆ per-`script` files under `scripts/` via **`emitScriptsForModule`**. Prompt `returns` schema validation (unsupported types, `returns` without capture) lives in **`validateReferences`** (`validate-prompt-schema.ts`). Tests and docs updated accordingly.
- **Breaking: `rule`, `script`, and `workflow` require `()` before `{`** ŌĆö Top-level definitions must use an empty parameter list and braces: `rule name() { ŌĆ” }`, `script name() { ŌĆ” }`, `workflow name() { ŌĆ” }`. Forms without `()` (e.g. `rule foo { ŌĆ” }`, `workflow default { ŌĆ” }`, or `script bar { ŌĆ” }`) are rejected at parse time with `E_PARSE` and a fix hint (e.g. `rule declarations require parentheses: rule foo() { ŌĆ” }`). Forms with `()` but without `{` on the same line get a braces-specific hint. All repo `.jh` fixtures, docs, E2E heredocs, and tests are migrated to the new shape.
- **Breaking: remove legacy interpolation forms from orchestration strings** ŌĆö Jaiph orchestration strings (`log`, `logerr`, `fail`, `prompt`, `return`, send literals, `run`/`ensure` args) now support **only `${identifier}` interpolation**. Bare `$varName`, `$1`, `$2`, and `${1}`/`${2}` are **no longer expanded** at runtime and are **rejected at compile time** with actionable `E_PARSE` hints (e.g. "use `${arg1}` instead of `$1`"). `$1`/`$2` remain valid **only inside `script` bodies** (standard bash). The `interpolate()` runtime function is reduced to a single regex matching `${identifier}` only. Compile-time validation (`validateJaiphStringContent` in `src/transpile/validate-string.ts`) detects bare `$name`, `$N`, and `${N}` with specific error messages. `extractShellVarRefs` in the transpiler matches only `${identifier}` for tree-display parameter extraction. Inbox dispatch now sets both numeric (`"1"`, `"2"`, `"3"`) and named (`"arg1"`, `"arg2"`, `"arg3"`) scope keys so `${arg1}` works in receiver workflows. All orchestration code, tests, fixtures, E2E scripts, `.jaiph/*.jh` files, and documentation updated to use canonical `${identifier}` forms exclusively.
- **Fix: strip synthetic outer quotes from `log`/`logerr` display** ŌĆö The parser now stores `log` and `logerr` message strings **without** their outer double quotes. Previously, `log "Hello $name"` rendered as `Ōä╣ "Hello world"` in the progress tree because the AST kept the surrounding `"ŌĆ”"` delimiters as part of the message text. The fix applies at parse time (`src/parse/steps.ts`, `src/parse/workflows.ts`, `src/parse/workflow-brace.ts`): `.slice(1, closeIdx)` instead of `.slice(0, closeIdx + 1)`, so the AST stores the bare content. The transpiler (`src/transpile/emit-steps.ts`) now wraps the message back in quotes when emitting the shell call (`jaiph::log "message"`), preserving correct runtime behavior. Output is now `Ōä╣ Hello world` ŌĆö inner quotes, variable interpolation, and multiline formatting are unaffected. E2E test assertions updated to match.
- **Reject shell redirection syntax around `run`/`ensure` steps** ŌĆö The compiler now produces an `E_VALIDATE` error when shell redirection or pipeline operators (`>`, `>>`, `|`, `&`) appear adjacent to `run` or `ensure` steps ŌĆö for example `run foo > file`, `run foo | cmd`, or `run foo &`. These are shell-level constructs incompatible with the Node AST-interpreter runtime, where managed steps are not shell commands. The error message suggests using a `script` block for shell operations and calling it with `run`. The previously skipped E2E test `96_run_stdout_redirect.sh` is removed; validation coverage is added to `e2e/tests/50_cli_and_parse_guards.sh`. The old `run ref &` + `wait` pattern for parallelism is superseded by `run async` (see previous entry).
- **Fix: correct progress tree depth for concurrent `run async` workflows** ŌĆö When multiple `run async` steps run in parallel under the same parent workflow, all sibling async workflows now render at the **same indentation level** in the CLI progress tree. Previously, interleaved async branches shared a single frame stack, causing the second (and later) branch to report inflated depth ŌĆö making it appear nested under an earlier sibling rather than parallel with it. The fix introduces per-branch frame tracking via `AsyncLocalStorage`: each `run async` invocation snapshots the current stack and runs against its own copy, so `STEP_START` / `STEP_END` / `LOG` events carry the correct `depth` regardless of interleaving order. Inner steps (`prompt`, `script`, `log`, etc.) align under their respective async branch. No change to sequential `run` depth. Covered by a new E2E section in `e2e/tests/104_run_async.sh` (`sibling_depth.jh`) that asserts both `Ō¢Ė workflow branch_x` and `Ō¢Ė workflow branch_y` lines have identical leading indentation.
- **Add `run async` primitive for managed parallel workflows** ŌĆö Workflows can now run steps concurrently with `run async <ref> [args...]`. Async steps start immediately (Promise-based) and are implicitly joined before the workflow completes ŌĆö no explicit `wait` step is needed. If any async step fails, the workflow fails with an aggregated error message listing all failures. `run async` is allowed in workflows only; using it in rules yields `E_VALIDATE`. Capture forms (`const x = run async ...`) are rejected at parse time with a clear error guiding the user to separate steps. The progress tree renders async steps with an `async` prefix (e.g. `async workflow name`). The old `run ref &` + `wait` pattern is superseded. Covered by parser/validator unit tests and E2E tests (`e2e/tests/104_run_async.sh`, updated `e2e/tests/97_async_managed_failure.sh`).
- **Fix: isolate workflow metadata env (no cross-workflow bleed)** ŌĆö Sibling workflows in a single run no longer inherit each other's metadata-derived agent settings. Each workflow receives a fresh clone of the parent environment before its own `config` block is applied, so `agent.*` and `run.*` overrides from one workflow cannot leak into a sibling. Additionally, same-module rules now inherit the calling workflow's effective environment directly ŌĆö module-level metadata is no longer re-applied for rules in the same file, preventing workflow-level overrides (e.g. `agent.backend`) from being silently reverted. CLI-level `JAIPH_*_LOCKED` semantics remain unchanged. Covered by a new unit test (sibling isolation in `node-workflow-runtime.artifacts.test.ts`) and E2E section 5 in `87_workflow_config.sh`.
- **E2E 90: rename `function` ŌåÆ `script`, verify argument forwarding** ŌĆö `e2e/tests/90_function_steps.sh` renamed to `e2e/tests/90_script_steps.sh`. All internal references updated: section titles, assertion messages, fixture file names (`function_called.txt` ŌåÆ `script_called.txt`, `function_args.txt` ŌåÆ `script_args.txt`), and shell variables (`function_out` ŌåÆ `script_out`). Test verifies exact positional argument forwarding end-to-end: quoted/space-containing args (`"one"`, `"two words"`) survive through `run` into nested workflows, rules, and scripts, with tree display showing `(1="one", 2="two words")` and file content matching `one|two words`. No runtime or compiler changes ŌĆö test-only rename to complete the `function` ŌåÆ `script` terminology migration.
- **Strict stderr-only `__JAIPH_EVENT__` channel** ŌĆö The CLI now listens for `__JAIPH_EVENT__` JSON lines on **stderr only**, for both local and Docker execution modes. Previously, `jaiph run` with Docker scanned container **stdout** as well as stderr for event lines, because the legacy bash workflow could interleave streams differently. With the Node workflow runtime now unified across all modes, the runtime guarantees events on stderr exclusively ŌĆö stdout carries only plain script output. The `wireStreams` and `drainBuffers` helpers in `src/cli/commands/run.ts` no longer accept an `isDocker` flag or parse events from stdout. `ARCHITECTURE.md` contracts section updated to document the single-channel guarantee.
- **Cache `buildRuntimeGraph` in `jaiph test`** ŌĆö `runTestFile` now builds the runtime graph **once per test file** and passes it to every `runTestBlock` / `test_run_workflow` step, instead of rebuilding it inside the loop for each workflow run. The import closure is constant across blocks within a single `runTestFile` call, so the cached graph is safe to reuse. If a test step were to mutate imported files on disk mid-run (not a supported pattern), the graph would need a manual rebuild. A new unit test (`node-test-runner.test.ts`) verifies that multiple blocks sharing the cached graph pass correctly.
- **Harden run-summary event contract: dispatch pairing assertions (e2e 88)** ŌĆö `e2e/tests/88_run_summary_event_contract.sh` now asserts `INBOX_DISPATCH_START` / `INBOX_DISPATCH_COMPLETE` pairing: every dispatch start has a matching complete for the same `(channel, target, inbox_seq)` triple, start precedes complete in file order, and required payload fields (`channel`, `target`, `inbox_seq`, `sender` on start; plus `status`, `elapsed_ms` on complete) are validated. Both event types are added to the `want_types` set so their presence is required. The canonical event contract is documented in comments at the top of the test file. This is a test-gap fix ŌĆö the runtime already emitted these events; only the E2E assertions were missing.
- **Remove `jaiph_stdlib.sh` and stdlib preamble from transpiler** ŌĆö `src/jaiph_stdlib.sh` is deleted. The file was the legacy Bash runtime library that delegated to `kernel/*.js` when workflow modules were executed as shell scripts; with Node-only orchestration it had no remaining consumers. `emit-workflow.ts` no longer emits the `jaiph_stdlib_path=ŌĆ”` / `source "$jaiph_stdlib_path"` bootstrap or the workflow entry dispatcher ŌĆö the `module` string now contains only Bash function definitions for compiler golden/snapshot test assertions and is not a runnable standalone program. `JAIPH_STDLIB` is removed from the default runtime environment (`resolveRuntimeEnv` in `src/cli/run/env.ts`); the `resolveBundledStdlibPath` helper is deleted. `package.json` build scripts no longer copy `jaiph_stdlib.sh` into `dist/`. The installer (`docs/install`) no longer ships or references the stdlib file. E2E helpers (`e2e/lib/common.sh`) and individual E2E tests drop all `JAIPH_STDLIB` setup. Compiler golden tests and fixture snapshots are updated to match the reduced module output. No production code path (`jaiph run`, `jaiph test`, Docker) sets or requires `JAIPH_STDLIB`.
- **Docker runs use Node workflow runtime (no bash workflow modules)** ŌĆö `jaiph run` with Docker enabled now uses the same `node-workflow-runner` process as local execution, instead of generating and executing a workflow-level `.sh` script inside the container. The container entry is `node /jaiph/generated/src/runtime/kernel/node-workflow-runner.js`, which reads `.jh` sources from the workspace mount and interprets the AST through `NodeWorkflowRuntime`. `prepareGeneratedDir` copies the compiled JS source tree and extracted script files into the generated directory ŌĆö `jaiph_stdlib.sh` and workflow `.sh` are no longer required. `buildScripts()` is now the only build path for all execution modes (local, Docker, test). The `build()` function and `emitWorkflow` module-string emission remain available for compiler golden/snapshot tests only. Docker args pass the source file path and scripts directory to the runner; `JAIPH_SCRIPTS` is set inside the container. E2E Docker tests updated accordingly. ARCHITECTURE.md diagrams and summary reflect the unified Node-only orchestration model.
- **Inbox dispatch parity: full channel dispatch in Node runtime** ŌĆö The Node workflow runtime now implements complete inbox dispatch behavior, re-enabling the previously skipped E2E suite (`e2e/tests/91_inbox_dispatch.sh`, 11 sections). Key fixes: sender identity uses the workflow name (not file basename); `send` routes messages to the nearest ancestor workflow context that declares a route for that channel; inbox files are persisted to `<run_dir>/inbox/NNN-<channel>.txt` on send; receiver positional args `$1=message`, `$2=channel`, `$3=sender` are forwarded correctly; `INBOX_DISPATCH_START` and `INBOX_DISPATCH_COMPLETE` lifecycle events are emitted with `elapsed_ms` timing. Parallel dispatch (`run.inbox_parallel = true` or `JAIPH_INBOX_PARALLEL=true`) launches all route targets concurrently via `Promise.all`; if any target fails, the workflow fails after all concurrent targets complete. Sequential dispatch remains the default.
- **Remove `jaiph build` CLI subcommand** ŌĆö The old `jaiph build` command (transpile `.jh` ŌåÆ `.sh`) is no longer a user-facing CLI command. `jaiph run` and `jaiph test` use scripts-only preparation (`buildScripts`) before Node runtime execution; the full `build()` path (module `.sh` + scripts) remains as an internal path for compiler golden/snapshot tests only. All user-facing docs, CLI usage, and examples updated accordingly.
- **Breaking: `mock function` ŌåÆ `mock script` in test grammar** ŌĆö Test files (`*.test.jh`) now use **`mock script`** to stub module scripts, matching the `function` ŌåÆ `script` keyword rename completed in the main grammar. Using `mock function` produces a **compiler error** with migration guidance (`"mock function" is no longer supported; use "mock script"`). This is a hard break ŌĆö there is no silent fallback or automatic migration.
- **Docs refresh: align with Node-first runtime architecture** ŌĆö All user/developer documentation updated to reflect post-rewrite architecture: Node-only orchestration, no user-facing `jaiph build`, scripts-only prep for `run`/`test`, and `mock script` in test grammar. Removed references to `emit-test.ts` (deleted Bash test transpiler) from contributor docs. Updated CHANGELOG to accurately describe current state of renamed/removed features.
- **Decommission Bash transpilation/runtime path: Node-only orchestration** ŌĆö `jaiph run` and `jaiph test` now execute exclusively through the **Node workflow runtime** (`NodeWorkflowRuntime` in `src/runtime/kernel/node-workflow-runtime.ts`), which interprets the parsed AST directly ŌĆö no Bash transpilation on the runtime path. The `JAIPH_NODE_ORCHESTRATOR` feature flag is removed; Node orchestration is the only execution path for all user-facing commands. **`jaiph test`** uses a new pure-Node test runner (`src/runtime/kernel/node-test-runner.ts`) that executes test blocks, resolves mocks (prompt queues, content-based dispatch, workflow/rule/script body replacements), and evaluates assertions (`expectContain`, `expectEqual`, `expectNotContain`) entirely in TypeScript via the same `NodeWorkflowRuntime` used by `jaiph run`. The Bash test transpiler (`emit-test.ts`) and its public API (`transpileTestFile`) are deleted; `validateTestReferences` is removed from the validator. The internal `build()` path can still produce Bash build artifacts (compiler golden/snapshot tests only) but is not on any runtime execution path and is no longer exposed as a CLI subcommand. Script steps (`script { ... }`) continue to execute as managed subprocesses (Bash or polyglot via custom shebangs). Architecture, CLI, testing, grammar, and contributor docs updated to describe the single-runtime design.
- **Fix: atomic step-sequence allocation via JS kernel (`seq-alloc.ts`)** ŌĆö Step sequence IDs are now allocated by a dedicated JS kernel module (`src/runtime/kernel/seq-alloc.ts`, built as `kernel/seq-alloc.js`) instead of Bash-side file locking. Under concurrent async branches (`run ... &`), each step gets a unique monotonic `seq` ŌĆö the previous Bash `.seq` file + advisory lock could race under parallel subshells, producing duplicate `seq` values and colliding artifact paths. The allocator uses the same `mkdir`-style locking as `emit.ts` and `inbox.ts` (via `fs-lock.ts`), reads/increments/writes `.seq` atomically, and returns the new value to stdout for the calling shell. `jaiph::next_step_id` in `jaiph_stdlib.sh` now delegates to `node "$JAIPH_SEQ_JS"` when `JAIPH_RUN_DIR` is set (fallback: in-shell arithmetic for non-run contexts). `JAIPH_SEQ_JS` is exported alongside `JAIPH_EMIT_JS` for child-shell visibility. Artifact naming (`%06d-<safe_name>.out|.err`) and `run_summary.jsonl` `seq` semantics are unchanged. The known-bug E2E repro (`async_prompt_artifacts.jh` in `e2e/tests/20_rule_and_prompt.sh`) is converted to a correctness assertion: 2 distinct prompt artifacts and no duplicate `seq` in `STEP_START` events.
- **Fix: nested metadata-scope inheritance for cross-module workflows** ŌĆö When a workflow calls `run alias.workflow` into another module, the callee now inherits the caller's effective metadata scope instead of re-applying its own module-level `config`. This restores caller-authoritative semantics: if `parent.jh` sets `agent.backend = "cursor"` and calls into `child.jh` which sets `agent.backend = "claude"`, the child runs with `cursor`. Three-way scoping: root entry applies full module + workflow metadata; same-module nested `run` layers callee workflow-level config only; cross-module nested `run` carries the caller's env as-is. `JAIPH_*_LOCKED` variables from CLI env overrides remain authoritative at all nesting levels. Prompt step artifacts (`.out`/`.err`) are now written with sequence-numbered filenames and embedded in `STEP_END` events for improved run artifact visibility. E2E test `86_metadata_scope_nested.sh` validates the inheritance contract.
